    634  3493
    635  3493							;-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    636  3493							; Player animation happens *every* frame so that we get good animation speeds.  Note that
    637  3493							; the player animation consists of running a small animation 'program', and then actually drawing
    638  3493							; the player.	The draw is the neat bit, because all it does is update some self-modifying pointers
    639  3493							; inside the actual draw kernel in the appropriate bank.
    640  3493
    641  3493
      0  3493					      DEFINE_SUBROUTINE	AnimatePlayers	; in GENERIC_BANK_1
      1  3493		       00 06	   BANK_AnimatePlayers =	_CURRENT_BANK
      2  3493					      SUBROUTINE
      3  3493				   AnimatePlayers
    643  3493
    644  3493							; Optimised 7/1/2012 -- single page tables
    645  3493
    646  3493							; This interesting code performs the animations for the player(s) and sets the
    647  3493							; pointers INSIDE the row bank for the draw code to point to the correct player
    648  3493							; shape.  Kind of neat, as it doesn't require any shape copying (=speed!)
    649  3493
    650  3493
    651  3493							; Cycle the player through his animation list.  The animation of a player is a direct
    652  3493							; pointer to the actual shape used to display the player.  This shape is in turn
    653  3493							; written to the current bank's self-modifying locations for the draw.  Since
    654  3493							; we are effectively drawing from this current bank, the same code can be used
    655  3493							; to 'undraw' the player as required.
    656  3493
    657  3493
    658  3493							; x = player index
    659  3493							; sets ManAnimation = FRAME to display for player
    660  3493							; ManAnimation = index of player program into Manimate list
    661  3493
    662  3493		       24 80		      bit	gameMode
    663  3495		       30 2c		      bmi	AnimationOK	; don't animate during pause
    664  3497
    665  3497		       c6 9e		      dec	ManDelayCount
    666  3499		       10 28		      bpl	AnimationOK
    667  349b
    668  349b		       a4 9f	   ReloadAnimation ldy	ManAnimation
    669  349d		       b9 00 f6    ContinueAnim lda	Manimate,y	; delay count
    670  34a0		       d0 07		      bne	NewFrameOK
    671  34a2		       b9 01 f6 	      lda	Manimate+1,y
    672  34a5		       a8		      tay
    673  34a6		       4c 9d f4 	      jmp	ContinueAnim
    674  34a9
    675  34a9		       10 0d	   NewFrameOK bpl	doDelay
    676  34ab
    677  34ab		       c8		      iny		; handle a REFLECT
    678  34ac		       a5 a2		      lda	ManLastDirection
    679  34ae		       29 f7		      and	#%11110111
    680  34b0		       19 00 f6 	      ora	Manimate,y
    681  34b3		       85 a2		      sta	ManLastDirection
    682  34b5
    683  34b5		       c8		      iny
    684  34b6		       d0 e5		      bne	ContinueAnim
    685  34b8
    686  34b8		       85 9e	   doDelay    sta	ManDelayCount
    687  34ba
    688  34ba		       c8		      iny
    689  34bb		       b9 00 f6 	      lda	Manimate,y
    690  34be		       85 a1		      sta	ManAnimationFrameLO
    691  34c0
    692  34c0		       c8		      iny
    693  34c1		       84 9f		      sty	ManAnimation
    694  34c3

      0  34c8					      include	"i2c_v2.2.inc"
      1  34c8							;
      2  34c8							; i2c_v2.2.inc
      3  34c8							;
      4  34c8							;
      5  34c8							; AtariVox EEPROM Driver
      6  34c8							;
      7  34c8							; By Alex Herbert, 2004
      8  34c8							;
      9  34c8							; Optimisations by Thomas Jentzsch, 2006/2008
     10  34c8							;
     11  34c8
     12  34c8
     13  34c8							; I/O Constants
     14  34c8
     15  34c8		       00 04	   I2C_SDA_MASK equ	$04
     16  34c8		       00 08	   I2C_SCL_MASK equ	$08
     17  34c8
     18  34c8
     19  34c8							; Signalling Macros
     20  34c8
     21  34c8							;  MAC     I2C_SCL_0
     22  34c8							;    lda     #$00
     23  34c8							;    sta     SWCHA
     24  34c8							;  ENDM
     25  34c8
     26  34c8							;  MAC     I2C_SCL_1
     27  34c8							;    lda     #I2C_SCL_MASK
     28  34c8							;    sta     SWCHA
     29  34c8							;  ENDM
     30  34c8
     31  34c8							;  MAC     I2C_SDA_IN
     32  34c8							;    lda     #I2C_SCL_MASK
     33  34c8							;    sta     SWACNT
     34  34c8							;  ENDM
     35  34c8
     36  34c8							;  MAC     I2C_SDA_OUT
     37  34c8							;    lda     #I2C_SCL_MASK|I2C_SDA_MASK
     38  34c8							;    sta     SWACNT
     39  34c8							;  ENDM
     40  34c8
     41  34c8
     42  34c8					      MAC	i2c_start
     43  34c8							; I2C_SCL_1
     44  34c8					      lda	#(I2C_SCL_MASK|I2C_SDA_MASK)*2	; 2	     I2C_SCL_MASK
     45  34c8					      sta	SWCHA	; 4
     46  34c8							; I2C_SDA_OUT
     47  34c8					      lsr		; 2	     I2C_SCL_MASK|I2C_SDA_MASK
     48  34c8					      sta	SWACNT	; 4
     49  34c8							; total: 12 cycles
     50  34c8					      ENDM
     51  34c8
     52  34c8
     53  34c8					      MAC	i2c_txbit
     54  34c8							; I2C_SCL_0
     55  34c8					      lda	#%0011	; 2
     56  34c8					      sta	SWCHA	; 4
     57  34c8							; set bit
     58  34c8					      adc	#%1000	; 2
     59  34c8					      sta	SWACNT	; 4	     SDA = !C (a = %1000 / %1100)
     60  34c8							; I2C_SCL_1
     61  34c8					      lda	#I2C_SCL_MASK	; 2
     62  34c8					      sta	SWCHA	; 4
     63  34c8							; total: 18 cycles
     64  34c8					      ENDM
     65  34c8
     66  34c8
     67  34c8					      MAC	i2c_txnack
     68  34c8							; I2C_SCL_0
     69  34c8					      lda	#I2C_SCL_MASK*2	; 2	     $00
     70  34c8					      sta	SWCHA	; 4
     71  34c8							; I2C_SDA_IN
     72  34c8					      lsr		; 2	     I2C_SCL_MASK
     73  34c8					      sta	SWACNT	; 4
     74  34c8							; I2C_SCL_1
     75  34c8					      nop		; 2	     required for timing!
     76  34c8					      sta	SWCHA	; 4	     I2C_SCL_MASK
     77  34c8							; total: 18 cycles
     78  34c8					      ENDM
     79  34c8
     80  34c8
     81  34c8							; Subroutine Macros
     82  34c8
     83  34c8					      MAC	i2c_subs
     84  34c8
     85  34c8				   i2c_startread
     86  34c8							; use V to flag if previous byte needs ACK
     87  34c8					      ldy	#%10100001	; 2	     eeprom read command
     88  34c8					      .byte	$2c	; 2
     89  34c8				   i2c_startwrite
     90  34c8					      ldy	#%10100000	; 2	     eeprom write command
     91  34c8					      I2C_START		;12	     start signal (clears V flag)
     92  34c8					      tya		; 2 = 16
     93  34c8				   i2c_txbyte
     94  34c8					      eor	#$ff	; 2	     invert data byte
     95  34c8					      sec		; 2
     96  34c8					      rol		; 2 =	6    shift loop bit into a
     97  34c8				   i2c_txbyteloop
     98  34c8					      tay		; 2
     99  34c8					      I2C_TXBIT		;18	     transmit
    100  34c8					      tya		; 2
    101  34c8					      asl		; 2	     shift next bit into C
    102  34c8					      bne	i2c_txbyteloop	; 2= 26/27
    103  34c8
    104  34c8							; receive acknowledge bit
    105  34c8
    106  34c8					      beq	i2c_rxbit	;43 = 43
    107  34c8							; i2c_txbyte: 264 cycles
    108  34c8							;-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    109  34c8
    110  34c8				   i2c_rxbyte
    111  34c8					      bvc	i2c_rxskipack	; 2	     previous byte needs acknowledge?
    112  34c8					      jsr	i2c_txack	;24	     transmit acknowledge bit
    113  34c8
    114  34c8				   i2c_rxskipack
    115  34c8					      bit	i2c_rxbyte	; 4	     set V - next byte(s) require acknowledge
    116  34c8
    117  34c8					      lda	#1	; 2
    118  34c8				   i2c_rxbyteloop
    119  34c8					      tay		; 2 =	2
    120  34c8				   i2c_rxbit		;	     receive bit in C
    121  34c8					      I2C_TXNACK		;18 = 18
    122  34c8
    123  34c8					      lda	SWCHA	; 4
    124  34c8					      lsr		; 2
    125  34c8					      lsr		; 2
    126  34c8					      lsr		; 2 = 10    C = SDA
    127  34c8
    128  34c8					      tya		; 2
    129  34c8					      rol		; 2	     rotate into Y
    130  34c8					      bcc	i2c_rxbyteloop	; 2=	6/7
    131  34c8
    132  34c8							; received byte in A
    133  34c8					      rts		; 6 =	6
    134  34c8							; i2c_rxbit:  40 cycles
    135  34c8							; i2c_rxbyte: 310/333 cycles
    136  34c8							;-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    137  34c8
    138  34c8				   i2c_stopread
    139  34c8					      bvc	i2c_stopwrite	; 2
    140  34c8					      ldy	#$80	; 2
    141  34c8					      jsr	i2c_rxbit	;46	     transmit no-acknowledge
    142  34c8
    143  34c8				   i2c_stopwrite
    144  34c8					      jsr	i2c_txack	;30
    145  34c8
    146  34c8							; return port to input mode
    147  34c8					      lda	#0	; 2	     0
    148  34c8					      sta	SWACNT	; 4
    149  34c8					      rts		; 6 = 12
    150  34c8							; i2c_stopread:  45/92
    151  34c8							; i2c_stopwrite: 42
    152  34c8							;-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    153  34c8
    154  34c8				   i2c_txack
    155  34c8							; I2C_SCL_0
    156  34c8					      lda	#0	; 2	     $00
    157  34c8					      sta	SWCHA	; 4
    158  34c8							; I2C_SDA_OUT
    159  34c8					      lda	#(I2C_SCL_MASK|I2C_SDA_MASK)	; 2	     I2C_SCL_MASK|I2C_SDA_MASK
    160  34c8					      sta	SWACNT	; 4
    161  34c8							; I2C_SCL_1
    162  34c8					      asl		; 2	     I2C_SCL_MASK
    163  34c8					      sta	SWCHA	; 4
    164  34c8
    165  34c8					      rts		; 6
    166  34c8							; total: 24 cycles
    167  34c8							;-------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    168  34c8
    169  34c8					      ENDM
    170  34c8

    801  3574							; calculate slot;

    820  358a		       20 d7 f4 	      jsr	i2c_txbyte	;6+264
    821  358d		       8a		      txa		; 2	     x = lower byte offset
    822  358e		       4c d7 f4 	      jmp	i2c_txbyte	;3+264      returns C==1

     80  3843				   CopyROMShadowToRAM_F000
     81  3843		       a9 f0		      lda	#>$F000
     82  3845
      0  3845					      DEFINE_SUBROUTINE	CopyROMShadowToRAM	; in INITBANK
      1  3845		       00 07	   BANK_CopyROMShadowToRAM =	_CURRENT_BANK
      2  3845					      SUBROUTINE
      3  3845				   CopyROMShadowToRAM
     84  3845
     85  3845							; Function copies a RAM prototype ROM bank into the destination RAM bank.  Typically
     86  3845							; the variable definitions are in the ROM shadow because this allows auto-initialisation
     87  3845							; of the variable contents from ROM declarations, but still allows access to them as
     88  3845							; variables when the correct RAM bank is switched in.	Code is also, of course, copied
     89  3845							; into the RAM destination so that code is callable whenever the ROM *or* RAM bank is
     90  3845							; switched in.  Further, if multiple copies are made to multiple RAM banks, then the
     91  3845							; code co-lives in all banks and may run even as bankswitching occurs between those
     92  3845							; banks -- by the very code itself.
     93  3845
     94  3845							; Note: Relies on ROM_Bank having being set via CALL mechanism to call this function
     95  3845		       85 b7		      sta	Board_AddressR+1
     96  3847		       86 d3		      stx	O_ROM_Source_Bank	; source bank
     97  3849		       84 bb		      sty	RAM_Bank	; destination bank
     98  384b
     99  384b		       a0 00		      ldy	#0
    100  384d		       84 b6		      sty	Board_AddressR
    101  384f		       84 b8		      sty	Board_AddressW
    102  3851		       a9 14		      lda	#>($1000+RAM_WRITE)
    103  3853		       85 b9		      sta	Board_AddressW+1
    104  3855
    105  3855							; Iterate 4 pages (1K) for complete bank copy
    106  3855
    107  3855		       a9 04		      lda	#4
    108  3857		       85 d2		      sta	O_CopyCount
    109  3859
    110  3859		       84 d4	   CopyPage   sty	O_Index
    111  385b		       a5 d3		      lda	O_ROM_Source_Bank
    112  385d		       20 3c f8 	      jsr	GetROMByte	; get byte from ROM shadow bank
    113  3860							;tax
    114  3860		       a4 d4		      ldy	O_Index
    115  3862		       a6 bb		      ldx	RAM_Bank
    116  3864		       20 4a f8 	      jsr	PutBoardCharacter	;6+21(A)	 write byte to RAM bank
    117  3867
    118  3867		       a4 d4		      ldy	O_Index
    119  3869		       c8		      iny
    120  386a		       d0 ed		      bne	CopyPage
    121  386c
    122  386c		       e6 b7		      inc	Board_AddressR+1
    123  386e		       e6 b9		      inc	Board_AddressW+1
    124  3870
    125  3870		       c6 d2		      dec	O_CopyCount
    126  3872		       d0 e5		      bne	CopyPage
    127  3874
    128  3874		       a4 bb		      ldy	RAM_Bank	; TODO: remove!?
    129  3876		       60		      rts
    130  3877
    131  3877
    132  3877							;------------------------------------------------------------------------------
      0  3877					      DEFINE_SUBROUTINE	SetPlatformColours	; in INITBANK
      1  3877		       00 07	   BANK_SetPlatformColours =	_CURRENT_BANK
      2  3877					      SUBROUTINE
      3  3877				   SetPlatformColours
    134  3877
    135  3877							; Now modify the hardwired colours so that we're correctly switched for NTSC/PAL
    136  3877							; The platform (0=NTSC, 1=PAL) is set from the right difficulty switch
    137  3877							; Note: This relies on DrawTheScreen starting on page boundary so that the (),y
    138  3877							; addressing will not violate the page-crossing restriction of 3E.
    139  3877
    140  3877							; TODO: adapt for fast vertical scrolling
    141  3877
    142  3877							;		  sty RAM_Bank			  ; we assume we called CopyROMShadowToRAM before
    143  3877
    144  3877		       a9 00		      lda	#<DrawTheScreen	; = 0
    145  3879		       85 b8		      sta	Board_AddressW
    146  387b		       a9 f4		      lda	#>( DrawTheScreen + RAM_WRITE )

    468  3991
    469  3991							; IF the creature runs out of time to do stuff, then rts HOWEVER the creature must eventually do something
    470  3991							;  as it will be continually called in available time-slices until it does. This can lockup the system.
    471  3991
    472  3991							; if the creature is done, and is alive next cycle, then jump ReInsertObject
    473  3991
    474  3991							; if the creature dies then jump NextObject

    929  3af9							;------------------------------------------------------------------------------
    930  3af9							; Look around is triggered by holding down the fire button for a while, without any other
    931  3af9							; joystick directions chosen. The variable LookingAround has a negative value ($FF) when looking
    932  3af9							; is active. Otherwise, it is counting down to the time where it will trigger.
    933  3af9
    934  3af9		       00 00	   LOOK_DELAY =	0
    935  3af9
    936  3af9		       a2 00		      ldx	#LOOK_DELAY
    937  3afb		       a5 92		      lda	BufferedButton
    938  3afd		       30 0d		      bmi	noLook	; button?
    939  3aff		       a5 a4		      lda	LookingAround
    940  3b01		       30 ce		      bmi	LookAround	; already looking
    941  3b03		       a5 90		      lda	BufferedJoystick
    942  3b05		       c9 f0		      cmp	#$F0
    943  3b07		       90 03		      bcc	noLook	; must have no directions chosen
    944  3b09		       a6 a4		      ldx	LookingAround
    945  3b0b		       ca		      dex
    946  3b0c		       86 a4	   noLook     stx	LookingAround

    157  788d		       b0 2e		      bcs	nextPhase	;2/3
    158  788f
    159  788f
    160  788f							; Process an object...
    161  788f							; Actual object code (the handlers) starts 82 cycles after previous segtime check!

    189  78bd							;---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    190  78bd							; Now process the blank stack.  This stack holds all the recently blanked squares
    191  78bd							; and determines (and moves) BOXs or diamonds into these squares.  The space vacated
    192  78bd							; by these objects are added again to the blank stack.
    193  78bd

    198  78c0
      0  78c0					      DEFINE_SUBROUTINE	SwitchObjects	;=72
      1  78c0		       00 0f	   BANK_SwitchObjects =	_CURRENT_BANK
      2  78c0					      SUBROUTINE
      3  78c0				   SwitchObjects
    200  78c0							; TJ: used by:
    201  78c0							; - BANK_FIXED.asm
    202  78c0
    203  78c0							; The game loop has come to an end. The only possible "still happening" thing is the sort, which runs
    204  78c0							; in parallel with other processes (objects, draw stack, etc). We may or may not want to wait for the
    205  78c0							; sort to complete.  This code does all the checks needed to switch to the next game frame.
    206  78c0
    207  78c0		       ad 84 02 	      lda	INTIM	; 4
    208  78c3		       c9 03		      cmp	#SEGTIME_SWITCHOBJECTS	; 2
    209  78c5		       90 f8		      bcc	EarlyAbort	; 2/3= 8
      0  78c7					      STRESS_TIME	SEGTIME_SWITCHOBJECTS
      1  78c7				  -	      IF	TEST_SEGTIME_SWITCHOBJECTS = 1
      2  78c7				  -
      3  78c7				  -
      4  78c7				  -
      5  78c7				  -
      6  78c7				  -
      7  78c7				  -	      echo	"***** WARNING! STRESS_TIME enabled @", ., "! *****"
      8  78c7				  -	      bne	. - 7
      9  78c7					      ENDIF
    211  78c7
    212  78c7							; If we're undertime, then abort. The sort will continue to run, and that's great. Only when
    213  78c7							; we're at the throttle cutoff do we switch game-frames.
    214  78c7
    215  78c7							;sec
    216  78c7		       a5 ad		      lda	Throttle	;3
    217  78c9		       e9 a0		      sbc	#MAX_THROTTLE	;2
    218  78cb		       90 f2		      bcc	EarlyAbort	;2/3		 plenty of time left!
    219  78cd
    220  78cd							; Time is up. But we may be in a level which requires perfect sorting
    221  78cd							; So we check for these levels, and wait for the sort to complete for those.
    222  78cd
    223  78cd		       24 ac		      bit	levelDisplay	;3
    224  78cf		       50 08		      bvc	keepFractional	;2/3		 screen does not require complete sort
    225  78d1
    226  78d1							; We have a level which requires the sort to go to completion
    227  78d1							; Check to see if the sort is finished...
    228  78d1
    229  78d1		       a4 c8		      ldy	sortPtr	;3
    230  78d3		       d0 ea		      bne	EarlyAbort	;2/3		 sort still in progress, so wait
    231  78d5		       a4 c7		      ldy	sortRequired	;3
    232  78d7		       10 e6		      bpl	EarlyAbort	;2/3		 sort still in progress, so wait
    233  78d9
    234  78d9		       85 ad	   keepFractional sta	Throttle	;3		 save fractional 'left over' bit
    235  78db
    236  78db							; Pause the game with B/W switch:
    237  78db
    238  78db		       a5 80		      lda	gameMode
    239  78dd							;		  ora LookingAround		  ; New behavour of looking around pauses creatures when activated.
    240  78dd		       30 14		      bmi	.paused	; pause flag set
    241  78df
    242  78df							; Now that we have completed processing the object stack, we switch
    243  78df							; the stack bank pointers for the next time around.
    244  78df
    245  78df		       a5 85		      lda	ObjStackNum	;3
    246  78e1		       49 01		      eor	#1	;2
    247  78e3		       aa		      tax		;2
    248  78e4		       86 85		      stx	ObjStackNum	;3		 swap stacks @here
    249  78e6
    250  78e6							; STOP the sort so it doesn't corrupt the "other" object stack. Sort may get a look-in immediately after
    251  78e6							; this code is finished, so we don't want it to do something unexpected!
    252  78e6
    253  78e6		       a0 ff		      ldy	#<(-1)	;2
    254  78e8		       84 c7		      sty	sortRequired	;3
    255  78ea		       c8		      iny		;2		 Y==0
    256  78eb		       84 c8		      sty	sortPtr	;3
    257  78ed
    258  78ed							; Initialise the iterator and stack pointer for next time around.
    259  78ed							; Previously the stack pointer auto-initialised by popping the stack. Now we have an iterator it's
    260  78ed							; necessary to initialise both.
    261  78ed
    262  78ed		       84 d0		      sty	ObjIterator	;3		 Y==0
    263  78ef		       94 86		      sty	ObjStackPtr,x	;4
    264  78f1
    265  78f1		       84 89		      sty	ScreenDrawPhase	;3
    266  78f3				   .paused
    267  78f3		       60	   quickExit  rts		;6

    375  7964							; Objects are unceremoniously dumped when there's not enough space.  This is just trying to cater

      2  7a15					      SUBROUTINE
      3  7a15				   TimeSlice
    581  7a15
    582  7a15							; FIRST check the time is sufficient for the smallest of the timeslices. Not much point
    583  7a15							; going ahead if there's insufficient time. This allows the previous character drawing to
    584  7a15							; be much smaller in time, as they don't have to include the timeslice code overhead.
    585  7a15
    586  7a15		       ad 84 02 	      lda	INTIM	; 4
    587  7a18		       c9 05		      cmp	#SEGTIME_MINIMUM_TIMESLICE	; 2
    588  7a1a		       90 d9		      bcc	timeExit	; 2(3)
    589  7a1c
    590  7a1c							; Uses the phase variable to vector to the correct processing code for the given timeslice
    591  7a1c							; Code may be in any bank. Avoid the fixed bank at all costs!	Once a section is complete
    592  7a1c							; it should increment ScreenDrawPhase.
    593  7a1c
    594  7a1c							; Switched-in bank(s) are undefined after this function is called!
    595  7a1c
    596  7a1c		       a9 06		      lda	#BANK_TS_PhaseVectorLO	; 2
    597  7a1e		       85 3f		      sta	SET_BANK	; 3
    598  7a20
    599  7a20		       a6 89		      ldx	ScreenDrawPhase	; 3		 current phase of drawing
    600  7a22		       bd ec f3 	      lda	TS_PhaseVectorLO,x	; 4
    601  7a25		       85 d2		      sta	TS_Vector	; 3
    602  7a27		       bd f1 f3 	      lda	TS_PhaseVectorHI,x	; 4
    603  7a2a		       85 d3		      sta	TS_Vector+1	; 3
    604  7a2c
